## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science / solid mechanics (thermomechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables (sigma stress, epsilon strain, T temperature) indicate a constitutive stress–strain relation with temperature dependence, typical of thermoelasticity, plasticity/hardening, and temperature-driven softening or phase-transition behavior in materials.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (1D linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear thermoelastic): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness changes with temperature)
- Thermal strain subtraction (thermoelastic with expansion): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (stress from mechanical strain after removing thermal strain)
- General thermoelastic with E(T) and alpha(T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * (epsilon - (c3 + c4 * T) * (T - c5)) (combined temperature-dependent stiffness and expansion)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (moderate-strain elastic nonlinearity)
- Nonlinear elastic with temperature coupling: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**2 (temperature changes both tangent and nonlinear stiffness)
- Power-law hardening (plastic flow curve surrogate): sigma = c0 * (c1 + epsilon)**c2 (monotone hardening with possible initial offset)
- Ramberg–Osgood-type implicit/explicit surrogate: sigma = c0 * epsilon / (c1 + epsilon) + c2 * epsilon**c3 (elastic-to-plastic transition captured by rational + power term)
- Exponential thermal softening of strength: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (c2 typically negative; strength decreases with temperature)
- Arrhenius-like thermal softening of modulus/strength (alternative to linear): sigma = (c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * T)) * epsilon (rapid stiffness change with temperature)
- Smooth transition across Tg/phase change: sigma = (c0 + c1 * tanh(c2 * (T - c3))) * epsilon (sigmoidal stiffness change near a transition temperature)
- Piecewise/shifted hardening with temperature-dependent yield (smooth surrogate): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1)**c2 / (c3 + (epsilon - c1)**c2) * (c4 + c5 * tanh(c6 * (T - c7))) (yield-like onset in strain and temperature-dependent flow level)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic regime identification: near-zero epsilon behavior often linear in epsilon; models with sigma proportional to epsilon capture small-strain response.
- Temperature softening/stiffening: decreasing (or increasing) slope d(sigma)/d(epsilon) with T is commonly represented by multiplying epsilon terms by functions of T (e.g., c0 + c1*T, exp(c*T), tanh(c*(T-c0))).
- Thermal expansion offset: if stress-free strain shifts with temperature, use epsilon minus a T-dependent term, i.e., epsilon - alpha(T)*(T-c0).
- Elastic-to-plastic transition: a rational term like epsilon/(c+epsilon) creates a smooth knee/transition from linear to saturated contribution, mimicking yielding onset without discontinuity.
- Strain hardening curvature: power laws in (c+epsilon)**n control concavity/convexity of the stress–strain curve and approximate many monotone hardening materials.
- Phase/glass transition behavior: rapid property changes around a characteristic temperature are well represented by tanh(c*(T-Tg)) or logistic-like sigmoids multiplying an elastic/hardening backbone.
- Coupled thermo-mechanical nonlinearity: if hardening rate changes with temperature, let the exponent or coefficient of epsilon terms depend on T (e.g., (c0 + c1*T)*epsilon**c2).
- Ensuring physical non-negativity: using (c+epsilon) inside powers and avoiding raw epsilon**c with fractional c helps prevent complex values and enforces sigma to remain real for epsilon ≥ 0.

**GT:** `7.723*epsilon**3 + 36.659*epsilon**0.2144*exp(-82.437/(8.314*T)) + epsilon*1.336*(T - 327.264)**2`

`epsilon*1.336*(T - 327.264)**2 = 1.336*epsilon*(T² - 654.529*T + 107,102.0)`
`= 1.336*epsilon*T² - 874.45*epsilon*T + 143,088.3*epsilon`

The GT has three fundamentally different structural components:
1. `epsilon**3` term
2. `epsilon**0.2144 * exp(-c/T)` term (Arrhenius-type with fractional power of epsilon)
3. `epsilon * (T - c)**2` term (which expands to terms with `epsilon*T²`, `epsilon*T`, and `epsilon`)

Key basis functions in GT: `epsilon**3`, `epsilon^0.2144 * exp(-c/T)`, `epsilon*T²`, `epsilon*T`, `epsilon`

Now let me analyze candidates systematically. Most candidates lack the `exp(-c/T)` Arrhenius term and the `epsilon*T²` term. Let me check which candidates could potentially match.

**Critical observations:**
- The GT contains `epsilon*T²` (from expanding `epsilon*(T-c)**2`). Most candidates only have terms linear in T (like `T*(...)`), which gives at most `epsilon²*T` or `epsilon*T`, not `epsilon*T²`.
- The GT contains `exp(-c/T)`, which none of the candidates seem to have.

Let me check candidates with `(c1 + epsilon)**2 * T * c0`:
This expands to `c0*T*(c1² + 2*c1*epsilon + epsilon²)` = `c0*c1²*T + 2*c0*c1*T*epsilon + c0*T*epsilon²`

The GT needs `epsilon*T²`, but `T*(c1+epsilon)**2` gives `T*epsilon²`, which is different — it's linear in T, quadratic in epsilon, whereas GT needs quadratic in T, linear in epsilon. These are fundamentally different basis functions.

**No candidate has `epsilon*T²`** — they all have at most `T*epsilon²` or `T*epsilon` or `T²` terms, but never `epsilon*T²`.

Also, **no candidate has `exp(-c/T)`** — some have `exp(c*T)` or `exp(c*epsilon)`, but not `exp(-c/T)`.

Since the GT requires both `epsilon*T²` and `exp(-c/T)` as basis functions, and no candidate provides both (or even either in most cases), none can match.

Let me double-check Candidate 8: `c0*epsilon + c1 + c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6*epsilon*(T + c7)**c8`
The last term: `c6*epsilon*(T + c7)**c8`. If c8=2, this gives `c6*epsilon*(T+c7)²` which matches the structure of `epsilon*(T-327.264)²`! The GT requires `epsilon**0.2144 * exp(-c/T)`, not just `epsilon**0.2144`. Since `exp(-c/T)` cannot be zero (it's always positive), and we can't multiply it in, this doesn't match.

After careful analysis, **no candidate** can match the GT because none contain the essential `exp(-c/T)` Arrhenius factor combined with the required `epsilon*(T-c)²` structure.
